Local News

Ministry of Communications' Determination

收回租界電話 125

To Recover Telephone Concessions

The Process of Consulting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: The issue of the Ministry of Communications taking back and self-managing telephone services in the Shanghai Concession has not yet materialized. Here are the letters from the Ministry of Communications to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs dated September 4th, November 8th, and December 11th of last year, as well as the consultation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on May 30th of this year, to show the Ministry of Communications' determination.

(1) September 4th, Public Letter from the Ministry of Communications to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs:

It has been heard that the Shanghai Public Concession Board of Works believes that the telephone services provided by the China and Foreign Telephone Company are performing poorly, and there is talk of canceling its contract rights and soliciting bids from other merchants. In the Tianjin and Hankou concessions, telephone services were initially run by foreigners, but were later taken back and managed by the Ministry of Communications. After repeated improvements, their performance is far superior to that of the Shanghai Concession's telephone services. Now that the Shanghai Public Concession Board of Works believes that the China and Foreign Telephone Company is performing poorly and intends to change the contractor for telephone services, this Ministry, responsible for improving and developing the national telecommunications industry, should seize this opportunity to nationalize the Shanghai Concession's telephone services in order to restore national sovereignty and facilitate public communication. Accordingly, this Ministry requests your Ministry to negotiate with the Shanghai Public Concession Board of Works to transfer the contract rights for telephone services in the concession to this Ministry, so that it can fundamentally improve them according to the spirit and experience of this Ministry in managing telephone services in the Tianjin and Hankou concessions. As for the original assets of the China and Foreign Telephone Company, their current value can be estimated and reimbursed by this Ministry. Your consideration and handling of this matter is requested, and the progress of the negotiations should be reported from time to time. Sincerely, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

(2) November 8th, Public Letter from the Ministry of Communications to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs:

Your Ministry's letter was approved, stating that in response to the letter stating that the Shanghai Public Concession's telephone services are performing poorly, it is heard that the Board of Works intends to solicit bids from other merchants. This Ministry intends to seize this opportunity to nationalize the telephone services and requests your Ministry to investigate and negotiate with the Board of Works to transfer the contract rights for telephone services in the concession to this Ministry. After the Ministry ordered the Jiangsu Negotiator to investigate and negotiate, the Negotiator reported back, stating that the case has been handled in accordance with the instructions, and that the poor performance of the concession's telephone services has caused complaints from both Chinese and foreigners. The Ministry of Communications has the responsibility to improve and develop the national telecommunications industry, and it is right to take over the management at its own expense for the convenience of public communication, etc. A letter was sent to the Shanghai Consular Corps requesting them to forward it for handling. The reply stated that after verification, the Chairman of the Board of Works replied that the current telephone services are indeed performing poorly, and that someone familiar with the matter will arrive in Shanghai on October 18th to investigate the current situation and prepare for consultation with the Board of Works, so it is hoped that all improvements will be made thereafter, etc. It is appropriate to reply for review, etc. In this regard, the poor management of the Shanghai Concession's telephone services is recognized by both Chinese and foreigners. However, the biggest reason is that the concession's telephone services are operated independently by foreign merchants with the aim of making profits. Therefore, telephone equipment is not replaced with new equipment until it is broken and unusable. Otherwise, the original old equipment will have no place to be disposed of, which is contrary to economic principles. The fact that most of the Shanghai Concession's telephone services, except for a few that have been converted to automatic, are still old magneto-type equipment is clear evidence of this. Therefore, the Chairman of the Board of Works' hope for improvement may be difficult to achieve. Furthermore, this Ministry is in charge of the national telephone system, which is very broad. If the Shanghai Concession's telephone services are taken back and managed, the situation can be assessed and improved at any time. The old equipment can also be moved and installed elsewhere for utilization, so that both construction and economy can be taken care of at the same time. Moreover, for the sake of restoring national sovereignty and facilitating public communication, it is imperative to take back the Shanghai Concession's telephone services. In accordance with the previous letter, this Ministry requests your Ministry to investigate the previous letter again and instruct the Jiangsu Negotiator to argue with the Shanghai Consular Corps to take back the Shanghai telephone services. Sincerely, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

(3) December 11th, Public Letter from the Ministry of Communications to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs:

Regarding the case of taking back the Shanghai Concession's telephone services, your Ministry previously stated that the Board of Works claimed that personnel familiar with the concession's telephone services would arrive in Shanghai to investigate and improve them, etc. A reply was sent to the Ministry, and the Ministry immediately sent a letter to your Ministry requesting you to instruct the Jiangsu Negotiator to argue with the Shanghai Consular Corps. Recently, it was reported that the Shanghai Concession's telephone services had been inspected by experts specially hired by the Board of Works and that foreign merchants would jointly purchase them. If this happens, not only will this Ministry's plan to reorganize and develop the Shanghai Concession's telephone services be shattered, but the contract rights for the telephone services will be lost to foreigners for a long time. Whether for national rights or for public use, it is necessary to take them back immediately. This Ministry, in charge of the national telephone industry, believes that if this opportunity is lost, it will be difficult to find a remedy. Accordingly, this Ministry requests your Ministry to investigate and handle the case as usual, and still hopes to receive a reply. Sincerely. May 30th, Consultation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Regarding the matter of consultation, this Ministry previously heard that the Shanghai Concession authorities had the intention of changing contractors due to the poor performance of the Concession authorities' telephone services. This Ministry believed that telephone services belong to the communication industry and are a type of national right. This Ministry, in charge of the national telecommunications administration, should seize this opportunity to seek to take them back in order to restore national rights and benefit the people. On September 4th of last year, this Ministry sent a letter to your Ministry requesting that negotiations be initiated to prepare for the repurchase. Subsequently, your Ministry replied on October 22nd without any results. On November 8th, this Ministry sent a letter to your Ministry requesting that the Jiangsu Negotiator be instructed again to argue with the Shanghai Consular Corps. In recent months, it has been repeatedly reported that the Concession authorities have been continuing to solicit bids, and the general method is that the winning bidder will use the funds to repurchase the original shares of the China and Foreign Telephone Company, take over the contract, and convert all the telephone services to automatic within the shortest possible time. The Concession authorities will grant them exclusive rights for 40 years and allow them to increase telephone rentals so that the annual net profit equals a certain percentage of the invested capital. The three bidding companies are all purely foreign merchants, and recently there has been news that the International Telegraph and Telephone Company is about to win the bid. The other two companies have objections to the China and Foreign Telephone Company's Advisory Committee's recommendation to accept the International Company's bid. Telephones are a public communication service, which is quite different from the business of ordinary buying and selling goods. In order to protect the rights of Chinese merchants, encourage investment, plan for a smooth takeover of the Concession, and reduce the burden on the Chinese people in the Concession, and for the convenience of communication between residents in the Concession and those outside the Concession, this Ministry cannot remain silent. Accordingly, a brief statement of reasons is attached and sent to your Ministry, requesting that you make a serious protest to the Consular Corps of various countries in Shanghai, urging them to make a decision as soon as possible to hand over the Shanghai Concession's telephone services to this Ministry for management, and declare to them that the Chinese government will not recognize any method of selling the China and Foreign Telephone Company to foreign merchants. At the same time, please appoint a special commissioner to work with the committee appointed by this Ministry to properly discuss and prepare the takeover methods to facilitate the process. Your consideration and handling of this matter is requested, and a reply is hoped for. This consultation is sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

楊樹莊談閩變 126

Yang Shuzhuang Talks About the Fujian Incident

The War Will Not Be Prolonged - Return to Fujian via Beijing is Not Confirmed. The Mainland News Agency reported that Lu Xingbang's troops in Fujian Province attacked the provincial capital, leading to a fierce battle with Liu Heding's forces. Yang Shuzhuang, the chairman of the province, was on vacation in Moganshan. After hearing the news, he immediately returned to Shanghai. There were rumors that he would go to Beijing and then return to Fujian. Yesterday, a reporter from the Mainland News Agency visited Yang's residence on Avenue Dubail and presented his card to inquire about the truth of the Fujian Incident and the current measures being taken. Because Yang was not fully recovered, his adjutant, Lin Zhijin, received the reporter on his behalf. The following is a record of the questions and answers between the reporter and Lin Zhijin:

(Reporter) When did Chairman Yang arrive in Shanghai?

(Lin) He arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday (the 9th) by express train from Hangzhou at 1:30 PM.

(Reporter) Has his health recovered?

(Lin) Not yet. Because of the tiring journey, all visiting guests are received by me on his behalf.

(Reporter) What is the truth of this Fujian Incident?

(Lin) I will not go into details. Everything is similar to what has been reported.

(Reporter) Can the battle between Liu and Lu be resolved in a short period of time?

(Lin) According to Chairman Yang's prediction, it will not be prolonged and may end within a few days. The central government has paid close attention to the matter since it started, and Yang also attaches great importance to it. Yesterday, he received telegrams from Acting Provincial Chairman Chen Peikun and Commander Chen Jiliang, both saying that the war will not be prolonged.

(Reporter) Can we know about Chairman Yang's current measures?

(Lin) After arriving in Shanghai, he has dispatched the Yongjian and Tongji warships and four seaplanes to Fujian to assist. He has also telegraphed Acting Chairman Chen and Commander Chen to take appropriate measures.

(Reporter) Is it true that Chairman Yang will return to Fujian in the next few days?

(Lin) He has not yet recovered and has no intention of returning to Fujian for the time being. He may have to go if necessary.

(Reporter) Is the rumor about going to Beijing true?

(Lin) There is no intention of going to Beijing either.

(Reporter) So Chairman Yang will stay in Shanghai for convalescence?

(Lin) That is the plan for now, but his whereabouts will ultimately depend on the situation in Fujian.

At this point, another guest arrived, and the reporter excused himself.

查禁外銀進口 128

Prohibition of Foreign Silver Imports

Crackdown on Smuggling of Foreign Silver - Unification of Trading Rights. Since the National Government issued an order prohibiting the import of raw silver, Shanghai's silver reserves decreased temporarily. However, recently they have increased greatly again. The reason is that many people are smuggling in silver, and some are trying to transport it through other places. As a result, the amount of foreign silver in Shanghai is increasing day by day, and the silver market is becoming more and more difficult to control. Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance has instructed the Jianghai Customs to strengthen inspections to prevent smuggling. In addition, because several foreign banks in the local area have been engaged in the trading of raw silver, Minister Song has decided to unify the import and export of raw silver under the management of the Central Bank alone in order to centralize authority and avoid abuses. This order will be announced within a few days.

(Notice Regarding Sanitary Rice: According to the Xinchang Rice Milling Factory, in order to promote public health and reduce food consumption, it is requesting that it be announced that top-quality sanitary rice is being sold, along with an advertisement stating that rice is an essential nutrient for the human body, and that nutrients such as protein and fat are contained in the rice bran. People in Shanghai only seek refined white rice for the sake of their appetite, without regard to nutrition, resulting in diseases such as beriberi, heart disease, and indigestion. Sanitary rice is properly matched, not sticky, rich in nutrients, easy to digest, and beneficial to health. It is also priced low, reducing one yuan per stone, etc. According to this investigation, the top-quality white rice sold in the market lacks nutritious raw materials and wastes food. After investigation and verification by this Bureau, it is true that bad habits should be reformed to emphasize hygiene. Therefore, this notice is issued.)

奬勵興辦公共事業 139

Encouraging the Development of Public Works

The Central Area Construction Committee, in order to encourage citizens to develop public works in the area, has drafted ten articles of measures, which have been submitted to the Municipal Government and passed by the Municipal Council. The text of the articles is excerpted below:

Shanghai Special Municipality's Measures for Encouraging the Development of Public Works in the Central Area:

(1) Any private individual or organization that develops public works in the central area, such as libraries, museums, and other public facilities that do not conflict with the nature of the central area and are not for profit, may request the Municipal Government to borrow public land for the construction of houses for the project.

(2) When requesting to borrow public land, the project plan and construction period should be submitted to the Municipal Government for approval.

(3) The area of public land borrowed for each public work shall not exceed fifty mu.

(4) The location, term of loan, rent, or amount of rent for the public land shall be determined by the Municipal Government.

(5) The public land shall not be sublet or changed in use. If such circumstances occur, the Municipal Government may take back the land and confiscate the buildings and all equipment on the land.

(6) The public works shall comply with all laws and regulations of the city and shall be subject to the supervision of the competent authorities of the Municipal Government.

(7) If the construction of the public works is not started within one year after the approval of the plan, or if it cannot be completed within the prescribed time limit, the Municipal Government may take back the land and recover the corresponding rent, unless there are special circumstances that have been permitted.

(8) When the public works are discontinued, it must be approved by the Municipal Government, and the borrowed public land shall be returned. All buildings and equipment on the land shall be taken back by the Municipal Government at a price to be determined, or demolished within a time limit.

(9) When the term of the loan expires, an application may be submitted to the Municipal Government for extension. If the Municipal Government deems it necessary, it may take back the public land or increase or decrease the rent. When the loan is taken back upon expiration, it shall be handled in accordance with Article 8.

(10) The provisions of these measures shall also apply to government agencies borrowing public land for the development of public works.

Arsenal Ammunition Loading Room to Be Rebuilt 140

An Interview with Director Zhang: After the explosion at the ammunition loading room of the Gaochang Temple Arsenal in this city on the 3rd, it is heard that the building there will be rebuilt. Yesterday, a reporter from the Kwok Man News Agency met with Director Zhang of the arsenal inside Gaochang Temple, who was surveying the foundation at the old site. The following is a record of Director Zhang's remarks:

Bidding for the Building Has Been Finalized: Zhang stated that there was a renovation plan for the building before it was destroyed, but it was postponed due to financial difficulties. Now, with the urgent need for military supplies, work cannot be stopped for even a day. Therefore, the building will be actively reconstructed. The bidding process was completed on Monday, with the bid price reportedly being 6,000 yuan. The plan is to still build three single-story buildings, but the area will be twice as large as before. The location is problematic because it is further west and closer to Longhua Road and the naval aircraft factory. If the old site is used, the obstacles of the armory make it difficult to design. Therefore, the site is still under survey, but a decision will be made soon. Once construction begins, the building can be completed in a little over a month.

Priming Powder Will Be Combined in One Place: The priming powder room was originally at the west end of the factory. However, because the priming powder and ammunition loading were close to each other, it was easy to cause danger, so they were separated. Now that the building is being rebuilt, it is planned to move the priming powder room back to one place, separated by an earthen wall to avoid danger.

Equipment Must Be Greatly Improved: In the future, the building will still be made of wood, not cement, because the stronger the ammunition loading factory, the greater the explosive force, which is the same principle as making bombs. Therefore, in the future, the roof and windows on all sides will be made of wood, but the inside will be divided into compartments with earthen walls. Each room will have a maximum of two or three workers. If an accident occurs, there will be no major sacrifices. The tools used during work must also be greatly improved to prevent danger.

Loss of Shenyang South Maru Arrives in Shanghai 141

Great Loss from Fire Burning Indian Cotton: The Japanese ship "Yangnan Maru" transported a large batch of cotton from India to Shanghai this time. A fire broke out when the ship reached the South Pacific Islands. Most of the cotton in the ship was burned, and the loss is estimated to be over 100,000 yuan. Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai, and a large batch of burned Indian cotton was also loaded onto the shore. The following is a report on the damage and follow-up measures:

Situation of the Fire: The Japanese ship "Yangnan Maru" was chartered by the Osaka Company, a Japanese merchant in this city, and sent to Bombay to transport a large amount of cotton to Shanghai. This time, a total of 8,150 bales of machine cotton and 6,000 to 7,000 other miscellaneous goods were loaded in India. The cotton in the ship was divided into six holds. On May 15th, when the ship was approaching Singapore, a fire suddenly broke out in the fourth hold. Cotton is easily flammable, and once it catches fire, it spreads very quickly. Later, the fire spread to four holds, and the fire was extremely fierce. The crew used all the water to put out the fire, and the fire was extinguished by filling the four holds with seawater, thus preserving more than 2,000 bales of cotton in the front holds.

Transport to Shanghai for Unloading and Inspection: After the fire was extinguished, the ship arrived in Singapore, stopped briefly for some repairs, and then quickly sailed to Shanghai for unloading. Yesterday, the ship entered the port and unloaded at the Linghua Warehouse in Zhangjiabang. Out of the total of 8,150 bales of cotton, 65% were burned or heavily water-damaged, with a total loss of 5,322 bales of cotton.

Handling Average Adjustment: When unloading the fire-damaged cotton and water-damaged goods, the Osaka Company notified the various firms in this city to send representatives to the site to supervise. At the same time, the public adjuster Haiming's Acheson was invited to the dock for inspection. It was estimated that out of 2,215 pieces of Shanghai goods, 624 pieces were burned. The remaining 4,000 pieces that were burned were purchased by Japanese merchants and reportedly resold to Chinese merchants. Currently, the company is handling the average adjustment as usual, requiring the firms to pay a portion of the average adjustment fee, which will be returned after the compensation issue is resolved.

Ship Repair: The ship "Yangnan Maru" was damaged by the fire, and the hull and nets were burned. It cannot sail on the high seas without major repairs. Yesterday, after unloading the cargo at the Linghua Wharf, the ship was scheduled to leave Shanghai today and return to Japan for dry docking. It is reported that the fire damage to the cargo alone amounted to over 100,000 yuan, not including the damage to the ship's hull. The firms and insurance companies have agreed to sell the water-damaged and burned cotton at the original dock in this city.

Important Shipping News 142

Tunan Collides with Japanese Ship: The Tunan of the China Merchants Bureau returned from Hankou to Shanghai. It first berthed at the Yangjiadu Wharf, and after the passengers disembarked, it sailed to Puxi. When the ship was in the middle of the Huangpu River, it had to turn around as usual. At that time, the river was very turbulent, and the Japanese ship "Shimizu Maru" happened to be there. The Tunan was impacted by the turbulent current and collided with the front of the Japanese ship. Fortunately, the captain tried his best to reverse, resulting in only a light collision. The deck canopy and other items on the Japanese ship "Shimizu Maru" were damaged. After the Japanese ship claimed compensation, the China Merchants Bureau immediately sent engineers with materials to repair the Japanese ship "Shimizu Maru" yesterday. Fortunately, the Tunan was not damaged.

Piece Goods Can Be Transported to Ningbo: Last month, Ningbo increased taxes on imported piece goods. The piece goods merchants in Shanghai had agreed to unanimously refuse transportation. After this incident occurred, it was closely related to the market. After mediation by various parties, it was determined that the tax increase was a regulation set by the Ministry and could not be easily withdrawn. As a result, the piece goods merchants in Shanghai canceled the refusal to transport the goods, and they are now being transported to Ningbo as usual.

China Merchants Bureau Builds Four Sichuan Ships 143

Costing a Total of 2.4 Million Yuan: Merchant ships sailing between Shanghai and Yichang have long been dominated by British and Japanese companies. This is because there are many reefs in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, and the river ships sailing in the lower reaches cannot sail between Hankou and Yichang. Zhao Tieqiao, the supervisor of the China Merchants Bureau, saw that the shipping rights were being taken over by foreign countries, so he requested approval from the Ministry of Communications to build four Sichuan ships, using gasoline engines, which are faster and more stable than coal-fired engines. The four Sichuan ships have already been built by a certain shipyard in this city, with an estimated total value of 2.4 million yuan (Continental News Agency). Gold Industry.

Exchange Limits the Amount of Tiao Method 144

Effective from the 16th of This Month:

No More Than 1,000 Tiao: The Gold Exchange yesterday notified the market that due to the current changes in foreign exchange and the indefinite rise and fall of gold prices, the Exchange, in order to seek safety and avoid danger, has decided that, starting from the 16th of this month, the number of transactions per broker per day for all August forward gold trading shall not exceed 1,000 Tiao.

Central Bank Inspection Report 145

The 56th Central Bank Issuance Reserve 56th Inspection Report states: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the Bank's issuance of convertible notes. The 56th inspection was held at the Bank's Issuance Bureau on June 10, 1920. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: The total amount of convertible notes issued is 17,285,710 silver dollars, including 16,158,719 silver dollar notes and 1,126,991 subsidiary currency notes totaling 12 silver dollars. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 17,288,311 yuan, including 12,318,705.2 yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves are stored in the Bank's Issuance Treasury at 9,127,700.033 yuan, in branch banks in various ports at 1,393,435.14 yuan, and in the same industry at 1,797,569.73 yuan. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 4,967,004.8 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is specially made on June 10, 1920, by Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank; Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiyi.

Bans Newspapers from Publishing Prohibited Advertisements 149

The City Social Affairs Bureau, in conjunction with the Public Security, Education, and Health Bureaus, has drafted six regulations to ban newspapers from publishing prohibited advertisements, such as those promoting obscene books and paintings, selling counterfeit medicines, and fraudulently soliciting guarantees by pretending to recruit employees, all of which are harmful to society. The regulations have been submitted to the City Government for promulgation. The text of the regulations is recorded below: Shanghai Special City Regulations on Banning Prohibited Advertisements in Newspapers: Article 1: All newspapers published in this Special City and those publishing advertisements in newspapers shall comply with these regulations. Article 2: Newspapers shall not publish the following advertisements: (1) Those promoting obscene books and paintings that are harmful to public morals; (2) Those promoting medicines with exaggerated claims that are close to deception; (3) Those publishing obscene pictures that stimulate the vision of young people; (4) Those enticing and deceiving with the intention of defrauding property; (5) Those that are激烈 and dangerous that prevent order and tranquility; (6) Others that are notified by the competent authorities to be banned. Article 3: Newspapers publishing advertisements promoting obscene medicines shall be handled in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on Banning Obscene Medicine Propaganda in this City. Article 4: If a newspaper believes that an advertisement is suspected of violating Article 2, Paragraphs 1 to 5 of these Regulations, it shall order the advertiser to first submit it to the Social Affairs Bureau for approval before it can be published. If it believes that it is suspected of violating Paragraph 4 of the same Article, it may order the advertiser to provide a reliable guarantee before publishing it. Article 5: Once an advertisement is published, the newspaper shall be responsible. If it is found to have violated any of the items in Article 2 of these Regulations, it shall be ordered to stop publishing. If it continues to violate the order and publishes it, it shall be fined up to 15 yuan or detained for up to 15 days in accordance with Article 33 of the Police Penalty Law. If it repeatedly violates the law and does not repent, it may be ordered to close the business in accordance with Article 18 of the Police Penalty Law. Article 6: These Regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Special City Government.

A Madwoman's Old Illness Suddenly Breaks Out, Two Lives Die Tragically 151

Tragedy in the New Puyutang Women's Hospital:

The Madwoman First Hits Her Head with a Porridge Bowl:

Then She Actually Took Out a Kitchen Knife and Chopped Two People to Death: Jiang Xu, a madwoman sent by the Second District Office to the New Puyutang in Nanshi on the 10th of last month, was kept in the women's asylum. Her madness had healed three days after entering the hospital, but the wound on the front of her head had not healed. At the request of her family, she was transferred to the women's hospital for medical treatment for more than 20 days, and there was nothing unusual. She even went to the door to buy things from time to time. Unexpectedly, her old illness recurred at 10:00 PM on the evening of the 10th. She first hit her head with a porridge bowl. When the female nurse saw this, she tried to stop her but was ineffective, so she went out and called a male servant to help. Then the woman actually took out a kitchen knife from the hospital's canteen. The patients in the same hospital were all terrified and fled. However, Gao Cailan (from Shandong) and Zhou Jinzhu (from Guangdong) were unable to escape in time and were dragged out and chopped randomly with the knife. When the female nurse summoned the male servants to come, the two had already been chopped to death. When the madwoman saw the crowd coming, she hid in the toilet pit in the patio, covered in feces. She was dragged out and her wrists were handcuffed to prevent another tragedy. On the other hand, the court was asked to inspect the scene. Yesterday afternoon, Prosecutor Yang arrived at the scene to inspect the scene and ordered the bodies to be collected. It is reported that the City Social Affairs Bureau received the news yesterday morning and Feng Section Chief and Rao Staff Member, together with Gong Staff Member of the Public Security Bureau, rushed to investigate and properly plan for the aftermath. All madmen in the asylum and other madmen's institutions will be strictly ordered to be isolated and seriously cared for, whether they are cured or not, to avoid unexpected events. Yesterday afternoon, at Xiaomuqiao Road

Murder of a Guardsman 152

Robbed of a handgun and over 300 yuan　　Was it for money or revenge?

Yesterday (12th) at 11:20 AM, a shooting occurred suddenly in the Sanjia Li area near Longhua Road Xiaomu Bridge in southern Shanghai. The deceased was shot five times and died on the spot. The details are recorded below:

Zhang Ziyan's Background 153

Zhang Ziyan, 46 years old, was a local of this area. He resided in Zhangjiazhai, west of Xiaomu Bridge on Longhua Road, southern Shanghai. He worked as an accountant at the Rihui Port Warehouse Wharf, Beipiao Coal Mine Company, and Xingji Accounting Firm. He was currently the executive member and standing committee member of the 5th District Organizing Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality Wharf Workers' Union and also served as a volunteer guard in the 2nd Defense Section of the 11th Team of the Xiaomu Bridge Guards.

Family Depends on His Livelihood 154

Zhang had a large family. His elderly mother, Liu, was still alive at 67 years old. His wife, Zhou, was the same age as Zhang. They had a son and three daughters. The son, Erchun, was 20 years old and studying in the third year of high school at Junyi Middle School on Guohuo Road, Puyudong Road in the southern city. The eldest daughter, Lianying, was 23 years old and still unmarried. The second daughter, Jingying, was 12 years old, and the third daughter, Yuying, was only 7 years old. The whole family lived in Zhangjiazhai in the countryside. Besides two self-built bungalows, they only had about two to three mu of inherited farmland. The whole family depended on Zhang for a living.

Suddenly, Thugs Jump Out 155

Because of his position as a union committee member, Zhang feared being envied, so he specially prepared a No. 11451 self-defense handgun, which he carried with him. Yesterday at around 11:10 AM, after finishing lunch at home, Zhang first went to the Guards for a short rest and then planned to go to Xingji Company for work. Unexpectedly, when he passed the Sanjia Li area, about one li south of Xiaomu Bridge, the place was extremely desolate, and the road was very narrow, only allowing one person to pass. Suddenly, two thugs jumped out from the side of the river.

Five Bullets Hit His Body 156

Zhang was walking slowly along the river when two thugs suddenly jumped out from behind, drawing guns and firing at Zhang. Five bullets hit Zhang's body, all in vital areas. He immediately fell to the ground, blood gushing out. By the time nearby villagers heard the sound and rushed over, the murderers had already escaped. They immediately rushed to report to the nearby Xinxiqu Second District Police Station. Officer Wang, upon receiving the report, immediately led the chief constable to the scene to investigate. At the same time, someone familiar with Zhang rushed to inform Zhang's family.

Died from Severe Injuries 157

Zhang's family rushed to the scene upon hearing the news. At that time, Zhang was still alive, so people carried him to his home, but he died from his injuries upon arrival. Officer Wang immediately telegraphed the headquarters and ordered the head of the local security, Sun Yongzhang, to report to the local court for an autopsy. The deceased's younger brother, Peiqing, accompanied Sun to the court to report. The deceased's brother, Zhang Peiqing, requested an exemption from the autopsy, but the prosecutor did not approve the request due to the seriousness of the shooting. He will send someone to perform the autopsy today. According to the family, the deceased also had over 300 yuan in cash and a self-defense handgun with him, which were all taken away by the thugs. The knife hole on his pants and

The Knife Wound on the Leg Are Different 158

Zhao Yunqing's cleverness backfires. Falsely reported robbery to embezzle money. The ruse was ultimately ineffective. The original banknotes were found on top of the bed.

Zhao Yunqing, 21 years old, from Hankou, was a shop assistant in Yongji Duck Feather Shop on Guohuo Road, outside Xiaoximen in the southern city. Yesterday morning around 9 AM, Zhao was ordered by the shop manager, Liao Zhifang, to take 200 yuan in cash to Yuancheng Money Exchange on Dou Street for deposit. Unexpectedly, after Zhao took a China Merchants No. 1 tram to the New Wharf and went into Lixiang, he suddenly encountered two robbers who stopped Zhao and robbed him of all 200 yuan in cash. Knowing he was being robbed, Zhao quickly grabbed one of the robber's hands and shouted for help. The robber then took out a sharp knife from his pocket and stabbed Zhao in the right leg. Zhao, in extreme pain, immediately let go, and the two robbers fled with the stolen goods. Afterwards, Zhao reported the above situation to the first district headquarters. After preliminary interrogation by the district chief, the case was handed over to squad leader Dong Mingde and detectives Yuan Haishan and Ren Shouzhi for detailed investigation. Then, Dong and others observed that the knife hole on Zhao's pants did not match the shape of the knife wound on his leg. The distance was also greater, which was suspicious. After repeated questioning, Zhao initially hesitated to answer. Finally, he confessed that when the manager instructed him to take the money to the money exchange today, he went upstairs and hid the money on top of his bed and then went out, took a tram to the New Wharf, picked up a piece of broken bowl from the roadside, and slashed his thigh, then used a knife to cut a hole in his pants, and then falsely reported to the district that he had encountered a robbery. He said that he had resorted to this trick because he was in financial difficulty. After the confession, the original banknotes were immediately taken from Zhao's bed and brought back. After the district chief's review, the matter will be handled further.

Worker Dies Tragically After Arm Is Severed 159

Careless work leads to hand touching the belt. Body is tragically rolled into the machine and killed.

Chen Jinlong, a worker at the Shenxin Yarn Factory at No. 36 Yangshupu Road, was from Changsha, Hunan, and was 42 years old. He lived at No. 299 Xiang'an Lane, Yangzhou Road. At midnight the day before yesterday, Chen was working in the factory when his hand was accidentally caught by the belt on the machine, causing his whole body to be pulled up and his arm crushed. He fainted from the extreme pain. The factory staff carried him to the nearby Hudong Hospital for treatment, but he died at 5 AM this morning. The Huishan Police Station sent Chinese Detective Zhang Desheng to investigate, confirming the facts. The body was sent to the Feilun Road morgue in a hearse. At 10:30 AM yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo of the Special District Court arrived at the morgue to examine the body and confirmed that the body was in the public seat. According to the report from the factory staff, they are willing to give compensation to the deceased's family and purchase a coffin. The deceased's wife, Chen Yang, also made a statement. Prosecutor Guo ruled that the deceased Chen Jinlong was indeed crushed to death by the machine belt while working. The body was handed over to the deceased's wife, Chen Yang, and the yarn factory was instructed to provide compensation. The Yang Kuihou kidnapping case

Verdict Announced for Bandits Yesterday 160

Zhang and Cheng sentenced to life imprisonment. The remaining bandits were given separate punishments.

Yang Kuihou, a compradore of the Dutch firm Anda Foreign Firm from Huzhou, was kidnapped on the night of January 10th this year after returning to his residence at No. 821 North Zhejiang Road from a brothel. His car was hijacked by bandits when it passed through Qunyufang on Shantou Road. After investigation by the General Patrol Room, it was discovered that the bandit's den was located at No. 905 Kader Road. Yang was rescued and the bandit Wang Caixi and others were arrested and brought to the Special District Local Court for trial. The trial concluded yesterday afternoon, and Judge Xu announced the verdict: Wang Caixi, Lu Weiting, Chen Deshan, Han Xiaowuzi, and Tao Wenzao were each sentenced to fixed-term imprisonment. Zhang Yaosheng and Cheng Dequan were each sentenced to life imprisonment. Lu Changqing's sentence was reduced to sixteen years of fixed-term imprisonment. Wang Lushi's sentence was reduced to six years of imprisonment. Song Xiaomei and Deng Lishi were found not guilty. The handguns, bullets, eyeglasses, etc. were all confiscated and destroyed. Auto Industry Discusses Price Increases 161

Effective from the 12th of this month. Shanghai's North-South Chinese and Foreign Automobile Industry, including 89 automobile companies such as Huang Automobile, Yunfei, Dalong, Hengfa, Yangzi, Xingfa, Yuegong, Dadong, Gongping, Zhonghe, Sanxing, Public Security, Da Zhonghua, Feilong, Hongkou, Zhongnan, Huishan, Xiang Sheng, Yi Tai, Da Zhong, Fu Tai, You Li, Tengfei, You Ning, Beiyang, Zhongxi, etc., have been repeatedly convening meetings of Chinese and foreign company managers to discuss solutions to the impact of recent gold price increases and high gasoline prices. As a result, the "Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Taxi Association" was established to implement increased rental prices. The price increase method is divided into large-sized automobiles, with a minimum rental of 20 minutes charged at 2 yuan per unit, and each hour at 5 yuan. Small-sized automobiles are charged 1.5 yuan for 20 minutes and 4 yuan per hour. The increase is scheduled to take effect on the 12th of this month (i.e., today). Penalties have also been discussed; any member of the industry who does not comply with the increase resolution will be dealt with according to the penalty rules.

Inspecting Users for Electricity Theft 162

Implemented according to the construction committee's rules for inspecting electricity theft. The Special Municipality's rules prohibiting users from stealing electricity have been abolished.

The Municipal Public Utilities Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating: Regarding the matter of the notice, the city's electric companies previously drafted rules prohibiting users from stealing electricity, which were submitted to the bureau for review and forwarded to the municipal government for approval and implementation. Now, according to the municipal government's order, the Construction Committee inquired and found that the electric power industry in our country has gradually developed in recent years, and the matter of users stealing electricity has also increased. There has been no uniform standard for the inspection of electricity theft and the recovery of losses. Most of the measures are independently determined by electric power operators, resulting in discrepancies in strictness and leniency, which greatly hinders the progress of the entire electric power industry. Therefore, twelve rules for the inspection of electricity theft and the recovery of electricity fees by electric power operators have been established to serve as guidelines. They have been reviewed and ordered to be promulgated and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. In addition to issuing notices to various provincial construction departments, ten copies of the rules are attached for your government to forward to the public and private electric companies registered with the committee for compliance. Accordingly, eight copies of the original rules are attached and ordered to be forwarded to the electric companies for compliance. In addition to ordering the Chinese electric company, Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, Pudong Electric Company, and Baoming Electric Company, which have been registered by the Construction Committee, to comply, the previously established rules prohibiting users from stealing electricity are abolished from today. This notice is hereby promulgated for general knowledge.

Union Secretary Training School Enrolls Students 168

Classes are scheduled to begin on July 1st.

The Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters, recognizing that the duties of union secretaries are very important during the period of political tutelage, and that while many incumbent secretaries of unions in the city are excellent individuals, many lack the necessary academic and practical experience, has planned to establish a Union Secretary Training School and appointed Pan Gongzhan as the director. The school's budget is estimated at 17,000 yuan, which will be allocated from the Labor Education Fund. The training period is set at six months, and no fees will be charged during the training period. A monthly allowance of 5 yuan will be provided. After graduation, students will be assigned to various unions for practical training, during which a monthly living allowance of 30 yuan will be provided. After the internship, students will be assigned to work in various unions. The enrollment process has now begun and the registration office is located in the Mass Training Committee of the Ximen Municipal Party Headquarters. The qualifications for application are limited to individuals aged 18 to 35, of good character and sound physical condition, who are members or probationary members of the Party and meet one of the following qualifications: (1) Graduates of secondary schools with certificates; (2) Graduates of senior elementary schools with three or more years of service and reliable proof; (3) Individuals with comparable education and two or more years of service as elementary school teachers with reliable proof; (4) Individuals with one or more years of service in a Party headquarters with reliable proof; (5) Individuals with comparable education who have made outstanding achievements in mass movements. It is also reported that classes are scheduled to begin on July 1st.

Attempt at Reconciliation in the Huashen Temple Lawsuit 171

Lu Shiquan, the manager of the Huashen Temple in Ximen Xieqiao, was sued by the Fresh Flower Industry Association, which was organized by the flower industry, for not allowing Lu to reside in the temple. Therefore, Lu filed a lawsuit in the local court against Wang Heyuan, a standing committee member of the association, for obstructing his rights and demanding compensation for damages. Yesterday morning, the judge opened the trial. Lu Shiquan stated that the position of manager of the Huashen Temple had been inherited for three generations. Since the establishment of the temple, it was originally a thatched hut built by the flower industry people for the purpose of worshiping the flower god, and there were no funds. The plaintiff's three generations managed and expanded it into eight flower sheds, making it the grand sight it is today. Since the defendant and others forcibly seized it, they have demolished five of the flower sheds, leaving only three. Only after the industry organized the Flower Industry Association, the plaintiff was commissioned as a receiving and dispatching person, with a monthly salary of ten yuan. Up to this year, he has not received a single cent for thirteen months. Now they are expelling the plaintiff, so he demands the recovery of losses: the three flower sheds in the temple are worth 600 yuan, and the remaining flower pots are worth 200 yuan, plus 130 yuan in salary, totaling 930 yuan. Defendant Wang Heyuan stated that because the plaintiff (1) harbored bandits while managing the temple, (2) often lost objects, and (3) was unclean and unhygienic, he was suspended. The official asked if the court could attempt reconciliation for you, provided that the plaintiff does not harbor outsiders in the future, is careful not to lose objects, and cleans the house every day to make it clean, then your expectations can be satisfied. The defendant said that although I am a standing committee member, I cannot make the decision. I should convene a meeting of the executive committee to have the right to make an agreement. The official then instructed that the executive committee should be convened within a week to report the decision to the court for review, otherwise a judgment will be made according to law. The court then adjourned.

Adultery and Extortion 173

Wang Lushi is extremely shameless. Wang Dianhuai is close to being a rogue.

Wang Lushi, a woman from Yangzhou, 43 years old, who lives in a flat in Wangjia Lane, north of Caojiadu, Shanghai, has a son and a daughter. The son, Guilin, is 23 years old, and the daughter, Aer, is also 20 years old. Although the woman is old, she is extremely flirtatious. She had a relationship with Pu A'gen, a blacksmith, last spring. The affair was discovered by her daughter, Aer, who became jealous. Then, the woman used a trick and married her daughter Aer to Pu as his wife to prevent her daughter from spreading the news. For Pu, it was killing two birds with one stone. In the spring, Pu married the daughter. So, the lover became the son-in-law. However, they still had an affair and secretly went to the woman's house to continue their old relationship. The neighbors all paid attention and were shocked. The other night, Pu went to sleep with the woman again. While they were having fun, Wang Dianhuai, a man from Shandong, broke into the house with two or three accomplices and caught the couple in the act. They tied them up with ropes. Pu saw that he had been exposed and repeatedly begged Wang for mercy. Wang demanded 50 yuan from him. Then, Luo Yingbao, an accomplice, mediated and persuaded the woman to pay 15 yuan. The woman agreed. The next morning (yesterday), Wang went to collect the money. The woman took the opportunity to run to the Guangfu Road Police Station and reported the incident. The police dispatched officers to arrest Wang and the other defendants, totaling five people, and sent them to the Sixth District Police Station. After separate interrogations by District Chief Ren, according to the plaintiff Wang Lushi, 43 years old, from Yangzhou, who lives in a flat in Wangjia Lane, and Pu A'gen, 23 years old, from Wuxi, who lives at No. 112 Xinmin Road and works as a blacksmith, and Wang Guilin, the son, 23 years old, from Yangzhou, and the defendant Wang Dianhuai, 26 years old, from Shandong, who lives in a flat on Zhongshan Road, and Luo Yingbao, 22 years old, from Anhui, District Chief Ren, after obtaining the confessions, determined that the case involved adultery and extortion and ordered that documents be prepared and the case be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Marital Relationship Is Cold 174

The wife once accused the husband and mother-in-law of abuse. The husband then filed for divorce.

Lu Yingquan, a local resident who lives in Miaotou, Zhabei, married a woman surnamed Jin from a nearby residence in 1919 through a matchmaker. At the beginning of their marriage, the relationship between the couple was still harmonious. In recent years, the relationship has become cold. Since then, there have been quarrels and even assaults. Because Lu Jinshi was repeatedly abused by her husband and mother-in-law, she felt resentful and filed a complaint with the local court this spring. After being summoned, the case was dismissed in court. Now, Lu Yingquan has also filed a personal lawsuit in the local court seeking a divorce. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Keqian opened the trial. First, Lu Yingquan stated that the defendant Lu Jinshi had repeatedly quarreled with my mother and even associated with hooligans, even colluding with hooligans to come to my house to cause trouble. My mother was afraid and hid in the bedroom. Those people smashed the door open and beat my mother, even smearing feces on my mother's head and face, causing her eyes to be injured. When I returned home and tried to dissuade her, the defendant was unreasonable and tore my clothes to shreds. At this point, he presented the torn woolen shirt and asked for inspection. The defendant Lu Jinshi stated that she was 27 years old, a resident of Miaotou, currently living in her mother's home. She married the plaintiff at the age of 16. At the age of 18, she gave birth to a child who died prematurely. She has no children now. On November 28th of last year, her husband and mother-in-law beat and expelled her. She had no choice but to return to her mother's home temporarily. Her husband had an affair this year and beat her on the 16th and 17th of January. I really had nowhere to complain. I was instructed to dismiss the case and returned to my mother's home. On March 21st, I returned to my husband's home, but my husband and his lover ate white rice while I ate wheat flour and was still beaten, told to marry someone else. On April 16th, the rice was cooked, but they didn't give me any. My husband's mistress runs a teahouse and hotel called Sanmei, surnamed Qu, and she is now living with my husband. On February 28th, the mistress gave birth to a daughter, so on the night of May 1st, the mistress entered the house. The official asked the plaintiff if he had an affair. He replied no. The official said that according to your statement, he beat the mother-in-law and still filed a complaint? He replied yes, because he went out to work and made sisters and worshiped the old man. The official asked if women also have old men? He replied that the old man is a disguise for the mother. The official asked how many households are in the same house. He replied five or six, such as Lu Baorong, Lu Xingsheng, Lu Houshi, etc. The official asked the defendant if she had beaten or insulted the mother-in-law. She replied to please ask the court to investigate the clan chief Lu Zhangquan and Lu Xingsheng, etc. I have not made any mistakes. He wants a divorce, I don't want it. Now, whether divorced or not, the plaintiff will pay 30 yuan per month until I am 60 years old. The official then attempted reconciliation for both parties, ordering the plaintiff to compensate the defendant 500 yuan for living expenses. The plaintiff replied that he had no money and could not comply. The official then instructed the two parties to reconcile outside the court for one week. If reconciliation is not possible, the court will schedule another hearing to summon witnesses and continue the trial. The court then adjourned.

Prostitute Without Shame 175

Testifying Frankly in Court Regarding the Assault on Her Cousin – Wang Yueqin, a private prostitute residing at No. 882 Hongxing Lane, Beijing Road, coerced 14-year-old Wang Yueying into receiving clients. Yueying, unable to bear the abuse, pleaded in vain, resulting in a severe beating by Yueqin, leaving her body covered in injuries. Neighbors, motivated by humanitarian concerns, spoke out against the injustice. The Lao Zha division of the police arrested Yueqin. It was reported yesterday that Yueying, originally surnamed Wu, was lured from Hangzhou to Shanghai along with her younger sister Yuegu under the pretext of finding work in a cloth factory. Yuegu, only ten years old, was spared complete corruption, while Yueying suffered not only from beatings with a stick on her legs and buttocks but also severe injuries to her private parts. Yesterday morning, the police escorted the two girls and Yueqin to the Special District Local Court, charging her with violating Article 249 of the criminal law. Presiding Judge Zhou Hanting conducted the trial, with Chief Prosecutor Zhou also present to perform his duties. Yueying first recounted her ordeal of being forced to receive clients and the beatings she endured. Wang Yueqin confessed that her cousin Yueying could not endure the hardship of working in the factory and willingly followed her into prostitution. She had recently received a Cantonese man who initially desired her but, upon arriving at her house, agreed to pay ten yuan for a night with Yueying. Because Yueying was young, she still acted on her behalf, sharing the earnings equally. Later, she beat Yueying for stealing money, not for refusing clients. The woman spoke frankly about her prostitution, seemingly unaware of any shame. After the trial, Judge Zhou sentenced Wang Yueqin to one year and two months of imprisonment. Yueying and Yuegu were temporarily placed in the Jiliang Institute, awaiting their family to claim them.

Introduction to a Sample of the General Catalogue of Four Categories of Books 179

The Shanghai Meibaige Road No. 121 Medical Bookstore compiled a General Catalogue of Four Categories of Books modeled after the Summary of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries. A sample edition was first published, containing a preface, compilation rules, a table of references, a book title index, a famous index, and selections from the four categories of classics, history, philosophy, and literature, with summaries totaling forty-nine chapters. Most of them are written by Qing scholars, based on factual evidence, which can be read as a sequel to the Summary of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries. Each volume only covers the cost of four jiao. It is sold on consignment by the Shanghai Commercial Press.

Japanese Ship Damages Coal Boat, Causing It to Sink 185

Wharf owner Zhu Jinsheng was carrying 22 tons of coal from the Zhonghua Coal Ball Company at 8:00 AM the day before. While Lao Da Tang Rongsheng and three crew members were rowing south, they passed the Nissin Company's wharf in Pudong. At that time, the Japanese ship Daifuku Maru was raising its anchor and sailing. The driver suddenly reversed the ship, causing the stern propeller to smash the coal boat's right side. The boat immediately took on water and sank to the bottom of the river along with its cargo. The four people on board were rescued by nearby ships and did not drown. Yesterday, Lao Da Tang Rongsheng reported the incident to the Customs Water Patrol Police for investigation. It is said that the loss of the boat and cargo is very large.

Dr. Xu Lizhou Not Guilty 186

No Neglect of Duty – Zhang Kecheng, a resident of Baoshan Road, Zhabei, filed a criminal complaint with the Procuratorate of the Local Court, accusing Dr. Xu Lizhou, a pediatrician across from the Xin Xiaocai Market north of Lao Zha Bridge, of neglect of duty. This case was previously reported. It is now known that the procurator has investigated the case and concluded that the doctor's guilt cannot be established. The disposition document states: "Zhang Kecheng claimed that his five-year-old daughter, Zhang Linan, fell ill in February of this month and was treated by Xu Lizhou four times, dying ten days later. Upon investigation, the prescription contained reed rhizome and polygala, which are contraindicated for the rash that his daughter suffered from. There is suspicion of neglect of duty, and he requests an investigation." Xu Lizhou testified that there was no error in his medication and presented Zheng's Treatise on Measles as evidence, which contains reed rhizome as a medicine. Zhang Kecheng also requested to withdraw the complaint. It is evident that Xu Lizhou's neglect of duty is not entirely true, and it is not appropriate to hastily recognize it as a crime. According to Article 244, Section 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a special disposition is made as follows. This case has been cleared." Mechanical Bicycle Race

Detective Team Arrests Robbers 188

The Chief of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, Captain Lu, was informed by detectives Xiang Shunbao and Han Ruisheng the day before that Huang Xibao and Li Asi, the robbers who committed the robbery at Yao Zhuqing's house at No. 142 Dama Road in the First District on March 10 of this year, were often found lurking near Xiaobei Gate on Minguo Road. He requested instructions. Captain Lu immediately ordered squad leader Fu Zhengcai and detectives Zhou Peisan and Wang Yao, along with Ding and Han, to guard the entrance of No. 959 Xiaobei Gate at 4:30 AM yesterday, where they apprehended Huang and Li. They confiscated a sharp blade used during the robbery. They also arrested Huang's wife, Li, and their two children in a house at No. 995 Minguo Road. After Captain Lu questioned them, Huang confessed that he was 32 years old, from Wuxian, and lived at Xiaobei Gate. Li confessed that he was 22 years old, from Ningbo, and lived at No. 83 Xiyao Lane, formerly working as a ship waiter. Both confessed to inciting a crowd to rob Yao's family and confessed to where they had converted the stolen goods into cash. The original detectives then took the two criminals to the Qingfuxing and Yuanfang Road Lao Baoxing silver shops on the east and west of the Public Concession Zhonghong Bridge, where the silver shops checked their accounts and provided written proof that they had exchanged goods for cash. After Captain Lu confirmed the facts, he immediately prepared a document and sent it to the Judicial Section for trial by the Ningbo Bureau.

Urgent Telegram Regarding the Detention of Domestic Goods Crepe Woolen Fabric 189

Yesterday, the Shanghai National Goods Factory Federation telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance, stating that according to a letter from Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Company, one piece each of Yuchengyutai Caishen Songbao brand crepe woolen fabric was transported by the Xinjiangtian Wheel to Ningbo on May 24. According to a letter from Ningbo, the Ningbo Fabric Unified Tax Bureau claimed that there was no record of this cargo and levied taxes on it as if it were foreign goods. The Ministry of Finance has approved our factory's products to be manufactured according to the machine-made imitation of foreign goods. According to the specific tax law, domestic sales are subject to a regular surtax at the first customs post, and no re-taxes are collected along the way. How can the Ministry's regulations be violated? Please telegraph the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance to order the exemption of taxes and release of the goods. The Ministry of Finance has approved the company's products to be taxed according to the method of machine-made imitation of foreign goods and holds customs waybills. How can the Fabric Donation Bureau arbitrarily levy taxes on the grounds that there is no record, not only exploiting merchants and people but also disobeying the Ministry's orders? Please order the bureau to not delay the re-taxation-exempted goods and to punish them according to law for contempt of the Ministry's orders.

To the esteemed editor of Shen Bao: I am writing to address the report of a strike at the Meiya Silk Factory in the local news column of your newspaper on June 11, which does not correspond to the facts. The factory workers did indeed stage a strike, which the Shanghai Municipal Training Council and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau jointly denounced, ordering them to resume work immediately. The workers who were dismissed—Lu Xiancheng, Wei Jiequan, and Zhang Fangyi—were illegal strike leaders who defied party and government orders and undermined the factory's operations. They were not four in number. The case has been submitted to the Shanghai Labor Arbitration Committee for arbitration. The Meiya Silk Factory has not changed its compliance with the terms of the Labor Agreement of 1927, as confirmed by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. The workers' request to revoke the temporary employment contracts is also unfeasible because the factory is required by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to have workers sign employment contracts. All disputes are being mediated by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau. No workers attended the first arbitration and mediation meetings, so the matter was not resolved. The workers staged a second strike during the arbitration and mediation period, which is illegal. I urge you to correct the inaccurate report immediately to prevent the spread of misinformation. I request that this letter be published in the local news column of your newspaper. Sincerely, Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, June 11.

June 12, 1930 (Shen Bao Local Supplement) Thursday (2) The Art World

British Novelist

D.H. Lawrence Dies 192

D.H. Lawrence, the British novelist known for his shocking portrayals of sexual psychology, has died. He passed away in March of this year in Provence, Italy, but news of his death has only recently reached us. Last month, Reuters news agency solemnly reported the serious illness of William J. Locke, a second- or third-rate British novelist in France, to the world. However, Reuters made no mention of the death of Lawrence, whose status and value far surpassed Locke. This may seem like a small matter, but it illustrates the lack of importance placed on Lawrence by his contemporaries and the cold treatment he received from his own countrymen. Lawrence has now become a figure in literary history, and his status and value will be determined by literary historians of this generation. We cannot know for sure at this time. However, because Lawrence was also a key figure in the modern literary world, one of the few important modern writers in Britain, we feel compelled to discuss this writer briefly now that we know of his death.

Nineteen Years Ago 193

Lawrence, the son of a poor miner and a graduate of a teachers college, published his debut novel, The White Peacock, after leaving the dreary life of a teacher to pursue literary creation. It immediately garnered praise from the artistic community and attention from readers. A rumor accompanied the book, claiming that the author suffered from tuberculosis and did not have much time to live. As a result, Lawrence's most notable traits at the time were his tuberculosis and his short life. These two qualities undoubtedly aroused sympathy for the author among countless readers. However, the weak young genius, who was said to be nearing death, actually fought tirelessly against death, only succumbing after eighteen or nineteen years of struggle. This was something that those who deeply pitied him at the time never expected. Nevertheless, Lawrence was never a healthy man. His illness not only caused him physical suffering but also affected his spirit. This influence is evident in his works. The unique sensitivity, anguish, hope, and passion of tuberculosis sufferers can be seen in his works. His extraordinary mental and psychological sensations and emotions inevitably make us think of tuberculosis patients. Many writers have been associated with tuberculosis throughout history. In Britain, Keats and Stevenson are two well-known examples. However, Lawrence was different from them. Keats, Stevenson, and others tried to separate their illnesses from their writings, meaning they tried not to let their illnesses show in their works. Lawrence, on the other hand, was not like that. His illness and his writings were intertwined, making them impossible to analyze. The characters he wrote about, the psychology he portrayed, and the world he described were all written with the heart of a tuberculosis sufferer and through the eyes of a tuberculosis sufferer. In the years leading up to his death, Lawrence lived primarily in warm Southern Europe and South America (Italy, France, Mexico, etc.) due to his health. The influence of sunlight can easily be found in his later works.

Pagan Blood 194

Seemingly in response to the sunshine of the south, and responding with intense passion, he seemed to see sunlight as a symbol of the path life should take. In his view, sunlight was a symbol of light, strength, freedom, and enjoyment. This was because, in recent years, he had increasingly felt that modern Western life was too gray and (against sunlight), and a life without sunlight meant decay and death. Therefore, in his collection of poems published last year, Pansies (unfortunately, this was his last work), he said something like this: (Conscience is the feeling of acknowledging the existence of sunlight and the instinct not to go against sunlight). This wild and eccentric Lawrence undoubtedly became a proponent of "returning to nature" in his later years. He lamented the disappearance of primitive life, the rampant materialism, and the harsh restraints of morality and etiquette. The increasingly gray and mechanized nature of human life and the gradual decline and suppression of human desire made him feel endlessly depressed. Therefore, he could not help but long for that free, bright, happy, instinctive, and primitive life. Lawrence's mood seemed abrupt at first glance, but we would not be surprised if we knew his history and circumstances. Lawrence spent his early life in England. He was born in the industrial area of the Midlands in southern England. The world around him was filled with gloomy coal mines, greedy people, and gray skies. His father was a poor miner. He dropped out of school after a few years and also became a miner. However, this intelligent and eager-to-learn young man was unwilling to live this kind of life. Later, through the introduction of Mr. Simon, a local teacher, he went to a teachers college as a scholarship student. After graduating, he taught in London for three years. However, this was also not the career he desired.

Ms. Guan Zilan's Solo Exhibition 195

Painter Guan Zilan will hold a solo exhibition at the Hua An Building from the 13th to the 16th. The image above is of her work (Portrait of a Lady). He began to pursue creative work. In 1914, just before the outbreak of the European war, his debut novel, The White Peacock, was published. Although it was only his first novel, his central ideas and philosophy were already evident in that work. If we were to summarize his philosophy in one sentence, it would be that we do not pay enough attention to our

On the Matter of the Flesh 196

That is, the aspect of bestiality. We subordinate the desires of the flesh to the qualities of the spirit, honoring the spirit and debasing the flesh, yet we do not know that the spirit is unworthy of occupying the highest position. Since he had this kind of philosophical thought, his works naturally contained many descriptions of sexual psychology and sexual desire. Such things were, of course, novel and bold in the British society, which was thick with gentlemanly air and moralistic sentiment. Although it aroused a lot of contempt and condemnation, this unknown young writer made a splash after all. His second work, titled (The Trespasser), was published in quick succession. The style and thought were completely the same as the first, but this book was rarely talked about. However, from the perfection of its style and the excellence of its form, it can be regarded as the best of Lawrence's works in terms of technique. His third full-length novel, (Sons and Lovers), is considered by many critics to be his best work. Some passages are written very beautifully and powerfully. The publication of this work increased his reputation greatly. (The Rainbow) is his fourth novel and also his first work to be banned. Even now, this novel cannot be openly sold in England. (The Rainbow) was banned by the authorities as soon as it was published. This was Lawrence's first conflict with the law, but at this time Lawrence was not yet a rebel with a clear awareness of opposing modern civilization. It seemed that the banning of his own works was beyond his expectation and greatly surprised him. Therefore, he remained silent for some time and dared not publish anything until four years later, when he published his fifth novel, (The Lost Girl). At this time, he was much more cautious in narration, but much more intense in propagating his views, especially in boldly advocating the concept of carnal desire. He believed that love should be based on carnal desire. If we all understood this point, we could be saved. From this novel on, he entered his second period. The novels he published in his second period were all bold and fierce, such as (Women in Love), (Aaron's Rod), (The Woman Who Rode Away), and (Lady Chatterley's Lover), which was privately published in Paris.

The later Lawrence's works became, the more they tended to promote his ideas, and therefore the more they neglected art. Therefore, his most artistically perfect novel is still (Sons and Lovers), which he wrote in his early years. His poems are also like this. The poetry collection (Birds, Beasts and Flowers), written in the early period, is so beautiful and keen, while (Thoughts), published at the end, is so crude and dry. Therefore, from the point of view of thought, the latter is valuable, but from the point of view of art, the former prevails. (Thoughts) is less like a volume of poetry than a book of random thoughts.

If we look at (Thoughts) purely from the perspective of poetry, it has no value. But if we put aside the outer form of poetry and pay attention to the thoughts within, then this thing is not only valuable but also extremely meaningful. As for the thoughts contained therein, they are of course completely (Lawrence's). Roughly speaking, it can be said that the world is already old, chaotic, and stinking. There is only fragmented licentiousness, no grand scale. There is passion, but only futile empty talk. There is no positive action. In short, this world has no order, no spirit, and no passion.

The World Is No Longer Masculine 197

All the dissatisfaction, instability, and culture and art in the world are the result of feminization. Women have destroyed us with unimpeded gentleness. We pretend to need us, but in fact, we are exhausted.

Because he felt that everything was feminized, he rejected all beauty. His meaning seems to be that before we can completely become free and masculine, we must remove all beautiful, gentle, and artificial things. For example, syllables, rhymes, diction, etc. are also in the category to be abolished. Therefore, we see Lawrence trying his best to write poetry (un-elegantly), seemingly deliberately writing his poems (masculine). As a result, the poems in (Thoughts) are of course very different from the poems we are accustomed to seeing. But this is not Lawrence's failure. This is really a concretization and centralization of Lawrence's thought.

Now Lawrence is dead. If we want to appreciate his art and thought, in addition to his several famous novels, (Thoughts), which has become his posthumous work, cannot be ignored. (Tiran)

Shaw's Wonderful Move 198

London News: The old literary giant Shaw recently received a letter from a woman saying that she had newly organized a women's group and asked Shaw to give away a free copy of his (An Intelligent Woman's Guide to Socialism) so that she could read it. Shaw wrote at the end of the letter, "(Tut, a women's group that cannot afford fifteen shillings to buy my book has no right to exist)." and returned the letter. Not long after, he received another letter from the woman saying that she had shown the previous letter to a bookseller, who accepted it and paid her with a copy of Shaw's book. Shaw replied, "(Foolish woman, if you had taken the letter to the appropriate place, you could have been paid fifty pounds)." and sent it back as well. Shaw also told people that he hoped the woman could exchange the second letter for fifty pounds.
